The GT contains three distinct basis functions:
1. `sqrt(A)` — a square root term
2. `A²` — a polynomial term
3. `sin(log(A + 1))` — a sine of logarithm composition

Let me analyze the candidates systematically by identifying which basis functions they contain.

**Key observation:** The GT contains `sin(log(A+1))`, which is a very specific transcendental function. For a candidate to match, it must either contain this exact function or something algebraically equivalent to it. No combination of rational functions, polynomials, exponentials, simple logarithms, or `sin(linear function of A)` can produce `sin(log(A+1))`.

Let me categorize the candidates:

**Candidates that are purely rational functions of A** (polynomials divided by linear terms in A): Candidates 2, 4, 6, 7, 8, 9, 14, 15, 18, 19, 20, 22, 25, 26, 27, 30, 31, 36, 38. These CANNOT match GT because rational functions cannot produce `sin(log(A+1))`.

**Candidates with `log(A*c+1)` but no sin:** Candidates 1, 3, 10, 11, 12, 13, 16, 17, 46. `log` is linearly independent from `sin(log(...))`, so these cannot match.

**Candidates with `exp(A*c)`:** Candidates 28, 32, 33, 34, 43, 44. Exponentials cannot produce `sin(log(A+1))`.

**Candidates with `sin(A*c + c)`:** Candidates 23, 29, 35, 37, 40, 42, 45. These contain `sin(linear function of A)`, which is NOT equivalent to `sin(log(A+1))`. These are fundamentally different functions.

**Candidates with `A**c` (power law with free exponent):** Candidates 5, 24, 39, 47, 48, 49, 50. Setting `c5=0.5` gives `sqrt(A)`, which handles one basis function. But they still lack `sin(log(A+1))`.

**Candidate 21:** Contains `c4*t/(A*c5 + c6)` — has a `t` dependence but the GT's `t` is already substituted as a constant (_t=7.144...). The rest is rational. Cannot produce `sin(log(A+1))`.

**Candidate 41:** `A*c0 + A*c1*log(A*c2+1) + A*c3 + c4 + c5*log(A*c2+1) + c6*exp(A*c7)`. Contains log and exp but no sin(log(...)). Cannot match.

**Candidate 51:** `A*c0/(A*c1+c2) + c3*log(A*c4+1) + c5*t/(c6+c7*exp(c8*t)) + c9/A`. The `t` terms become constants (since `t` is fixed). This gives a rational function of A plus log(A*c4+1) plus 1/A. Cannot produce `sin(log(A+1))`.

**Conclusion:** None of the candidates contain the basis function `sin(log(A+c))`. The GT fundamentally requires this transcendental composition, and it cannot be represented by any combination of:
- Rational functions of A
- Simple logarithms `log(A+c)`
- Exponentials `exp(cA)`
- `sin(linear function of A)`
- Power laws `A^c`

Since `sin(log(A+1))` is linearly independent from all these function classes, no candidate can match the GT.
